 acti
makes an argument that persuades his audience that natural darkness should be preserved. He uses evidence, reasoning, and stylistic or persuasive elements to support his claims,  to support his claims  to develop ideas and to connect claims and evidence add power to his arguments.
	 	 	 
 In the first paragraph, Bogard describes his experience as a young in the woodat night in with his family to persuade .  This is a stylistic elem
ent meant to draw the reader in and also to give the reader an understanding of the experienchow great darkness is. And then he lets it And then he gives a shocking statistic that 8 of 10 children born in the United States will never know a sky dark enough for the Milky Wayth, which supports his argument that we are losing darkness and natural should preserve it. 
	 
The second paragraph, Bogard uses reasoning and stylistic elements and reasoning to strengthen his argument and ma  and justify ..  in the second paragraph "All life e The first sentence isHe reasons that since fore most in the past, we all experienced a steady light of day nessthe and darkness of night, and now we have easy access to artificial an overwhelming abundance of artificial light, we must be exposed to too much light and too little darkness, which is a bad thing. The second pa He says this in a convincing way that  This establishes the idea that it is natural for there to be natural of a natural light day and dark night ly s ,  naturals, and makes readers understand why light polltion is such a pr that reminds makes his argument more powerful: the first sentence asserts that all life evolved to the steady rythm of bright days andthe steady rythm of bright days and dark nights."" The second sentence contrasts this with the prevalence "Steady rhythm" makes natural lightness and darkness seem goodwhile "we reach quickly fore and is contrasted wi a light switch": one is slow and steady, while the other is fast and unpredictable.
The fourth paragraph asserts that all life depends on darkness and gives examples of this. Bogard  gives an example of the usefullness of evidence value darkness One piece of that Bogard gives is the fact that bats save American farmers billions in pest control because of the bats that why depend on darkness. This stresses even more the importance of darkness. In the same paragraph, a similie comparing light pollution to a bulldozer owrecking habitat adds power to the topic of the paragraph paragraph's subject, that the world depends on darkness. —a perssive element The last sentence employs another stylistic element: "without darkness, Earth's ecology would collapse."
  This adds huge power to the argument of the paragraph, that the world's life depends on darkness, and of the essay, that darkness is invaluable and must be preserved.
Bogard did a great job in convincing his readers that light pollution is really bad and that it must be stopped and recognized with his use of styllistic elements and evidence.  and rea (6/24^/2(3=2^(3x-y)=2^12^))1y)+4+6) gimp

.From a Raw Deal to a NEw Deal By William Trotter, Jr.
Surface meaning:
It is about the situation of African Americans in the great depression era. It mentions that Blacks had a higher unemployment rate than whites, that whites competed for Black people's jobs. It is about the situation for Blacks in terms of jobs, economics, and politics. Also talks about the Hoover aned FDR administrations and how they both did not help the Black people. Blacks moved to cities
Could have been said but wasn't:
What other people think/thought about why FDR didn't support African Americans and why FDR didn't do this. About the white people's situation and why they were trying to take black people's jobs.

	Biases:

rash in 1929

Racial lens, economic lens, Marxist lens

/**
Generates a sample of a sound wave with the desired timbre.
@param f the frequency of the wave
@param a the amplitude of the wave timbre
 
@param x time in seconds since the beginning of the wave
@param freqAndAmps the frequencies and corresponding dB amplitudes of sines to sum. Gives wave its timbre.
@p
 originalFreq the original frequency of the sound. Usually the loudest frequency in the spectrum. Allows for pitch change.

 pa page It mentions that Blacks . IIt doesn't say what happened in the stock market crash in 1929. Therefore it assumes that the reader knows about this. It uses a racial lens, evident in it looking at the situation of Blacks, ad compared to whites, and it also uses an economic lens by analyzing finacnial situations. It also uses a "Marxist lens by looking at class " , etc..instead they selectively choose what things to include and not include to create a coherent story that conforms to the topic they are writing about and "lenses" they are usin It doesn't say what , or   Although no biases were immediately evident, there could have been a bias in favor of Black peopl The passage uses a race lens, since it focuses on "black and "white" people. It also uses a class lens, or a marxist lens: it looks at the proletariat, the capitalists, and on strikebreake 
This passage is from a book about the history of America's women. The chapter is on the greate d GreaDepression. It talks about a range of things, including how living standards dropped for most everyone. It says that the middle class worried about losing their homew and that rich people lost servants. It also talks about what happened when contraceptives were made legal: a lower birthrate, a decrease in divorce, and an increase in abandonment rates.  It talks about how the poor got poorer and how the poor suffered the most. Due to this, it says, solidarity among the poor was often strong. It mentions how the low job opportunities caused people to try to convince married women to stay at home in order to increase employment opportunities. And lastly, it explains the New Deal electrification program. It says this program was the New Deal program that had the highest impact on the most women because it lead to a change in lifestyle among rural women. 
 This didn't mention anything about the presidents or Roosevelt's strategy for making what is described happen. It also could have mentioned what other New Deal programs there were. It could have mentioned what the Great Depression pro other grams there were. It could have mentioned what the Great Depression did to different raece groups. race  It covered talked about I can tell that it This passage seems to be middle and upper-class centric since it talks more about these people and has them in the introduction. It assumes that the world was divided into male and feamale jobs. This may have been the case for the United States, but I'm not so sure about the rest of the world.  There Te historian assumes that the Great Depression  ended in 1941. It also assumes that the reader knows about the Great Depression's causes andsimilar backgroun  based on data
 
 and people lived in "Hoovervilles" (villages made of shcks built on garbage dumps). It goes into great length describing the rebellion of the poor protesting shortages of work and food. It also tells us what FDR's reforms were meant to do: "reorganize capitalism to overcome the crisis and stabilize the system" and to head off the "growth of spontaneous rebellion" and how he did this: the National Recovery Act (NRA) and teh Agricultural the Adjustment Administration (AAA), among others.
It didn't say what happened to the middle and upper class. It didn't use a race lens or a gender lens. It also could have said about the success of the New Deal: how many of the end goals for the New Deal were met? A possible bias this had was a bias that poor people were more important or significant than other people. Zinn looked at the jobs people had—workers, or politicians, rpg

   A game called Kingdom Come: Deliverance hired a historian named Joanna Nowak  to make the game more historically accurate.
 In-house historical consultants are common in film and televisioin but rare in the development of games. 
 When the game developers asked her what the game should look like to be  an aspect of historically accurate, Nowak didn't always know the answer , so she had to make the best decisions she could based on her research. 
 The game wasn't meant to be completely historically accurate  to the time period 1403 Bohemia  – they had to balance historical accuracy with engagement. 
 
 Kingdom Come: Deliverance has the potential to engage people in history d  get players more interested  because it is like a living in the game is  the game is based on history. 
 The game has the  potential to get This 's details are ,  i after they plaThe game raised more than 1.1 million pounds on KickstarterIn 2014, .in a campaign Now the game has more The game has more people working on it now than in 2014.Crowdfunding gamesB Its Kickstarter campaign allowed it to the developers to try new thingsThe money raisted through the game'sraised in how they made the game, like hiring a historian to make the game more historically accurate. This will influencecan other game makers to coulduse their money to do new things.In an effort to make their game as true to history as possible, Warhorse Studios hired a historian to make the help them make their game as true to history as they could without ruining the fun – a rare endeavor in the development of videogames.Video Games

4. If I had to create a high school course the focus would be machine learning. Machine learning is a field of computer science in which people deviand a type of artificial intelligence. Machine learning is when a computer learns from data, can improve by trial and error,  itself and it can be implemented with various algorithms such as neural networks or genetic algorithms. The course would involve both theory and practice, with an emphasis on practice through tutorials. I am interested in teaching this course because I have found that it is challenging to explore machine learning, due to the complex math involved. My goal is to make it easier for high school students who are interested in machine learning to implement algorithms.

There is a link between video games and unemployment.  The article reflects on a paper suggesting that high-quality video games are contributing to a decline in work among young peop It comes to the conclusion that spending tiemyoung people  playing video gamesmore  is a symptom of unemployment rather than the other way round.
vice versa
vice versaFor each hour less the group In the paper which the article studies Tsays that for each hour that men in their 20s without a college education spent less in work, time spent on leasure actiiities rose by about an hour – 75% of which was spent on gaming.
It justifies this factThe article then makes the point that  and supplies evidence forthe factlabour-market options for young people got worse.brings e since the turn of the century while games impro"while games improved since the turn of the century, labour-market options for young people got worse."W
From this it then concludes that young people spending more time on video games is a symspend more time on video games when job opporunities are bleak, rather than the other way round.
 
Simply put, the article brings up several intertwines pieces of evidence with a narritive concludes that In summary argues  brings up evi young people are playing more spending time playing video games, video games job opporunities got worse since 2000, and got better since 2000, becau the yea.. getting  cause spend to  moreleasure , much of that time spend  in part because video games got better since the year 200 spent for the reason — and  ,  wa;
This article conviThe argument made in the aThis premise may influence people to focus on the problem of young men getting distracted by video games causeless and more on the problem of decreased job opportunities for young people causing them to play video games.
 moreThis is a good thing because And this influenceknowing what the problem is is This could be more effectual in getting young people to work more Using this approachand play less video gaming waste less time . Not that video games are always a waste of time, but I think you can agree with me that making money comes before  to provide for oneselfleisure activities such as video games.
